The Fourth Argument: Heat as the Source of Sensation and Voluntary Movement
Al-Razi argues that heat (from heart) is the source of perception and motion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Razi's fourth proof that the heart, not the brain, is the principle of sensation and voluntary movement, based on the causal role of heat.

Core Idea
Heat enables sensation and movement; cold hinders them.

Al-Razi presents a physiological argument to locate the rational soul in the heart. He argues that sensation and voluntary movement rely on heat, and that the heart is the body's source of heat. Therefore, the heart is more fitting as their source than the brain, which is associated with cold. This argument combines empirical medical observations with a causal principle.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the clear structure: premise, evidence, conclusion.
2
Identify the key claim about heat and cold
Find the statement that sensation and movement are obtained only by heat, and that cold hinders them. This is the foundational premise.
3
Notice the use of medical experiments as evidence
Al-Razi cites 'tajārib ṭibbiyya' (medical experiments) as support. Consider why this empirical appeal strengthens the argument.
This shows the argument is not purely theoretical.
4
Follow the conclusion about heart vs. brain
The argument then identifies the heart as the source of heat and the brain as the source of cold, leading to the conclusion that the heart is more appropriate as the principle (mabda’) of sensation and movement.
The reasoning is: heat causes these functions → heart supplies heat → heart is the principle.
5
Reflect on the reasoning structure
Consider how the argument moves from a general causal claim to a specific anatomical conclusion. This is a deductive argument with empirical backing.
This type of reasoning is common in kalām discussions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الرابعة : إن الحس والحركة الإرادية، إنما تحصل بالحرارة : وأما البرودة فعائقة عنهما ، ويدل على صحة ما ذكرناه : التجارب الطبية ، وإذا ثبت هذا ، فنقول : القلب منبع للحرارة ، والدماغ منبع للبرودة . فجعل القلب منبعاً للحس والحركة الإرادية أولى من جعل الدماغ مبدأ لهما .
The fourth proof: Verily, sensation and voluntary movement are obtained only by heat. As for cold, it hinders them. Medical experiments indicate the correctness of what we have mentioned. And if this is established, we say: The heart is the source of heat, and the brain is the source of cold. So making the heart the source of sensation and voluntary movement is more appropriate than making the brain the principle of them.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage is a self-contained argument, the fourth proof (al-hujja al-rabi'a) in a series defending the view that the rational soul resides in the heart. The argument is causal: it begins by asserting that sensation and voluntary movement (al-hiss wa al-haraka al-iradiyya) are produced only by heat (al-harara), while cold (al-baruda) impedes them. Medical experiments are cited as confirming this. From this premise, the author concludes that the heart is the source (manba‘) of heat and the brain the source of cold. Therefore, it is more fitting (awlā) to attribute the origin of sensation and movement to the heart rather than to the brain, since the cause of an effect should be traced to its true source. The reasoning is straightforward: heat causes perception/motion, heart supplies heat, so heart is the principle (mabda’).

The Fifth Argument: Pointing to the Heart
Al-Razi uses the universal human gesture of pointing to the chest as evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Razi uses a universal human gesture as evidence for the location of the self in the heart.

Core Idea
Universal gesture reveals innate knowledge of the self's seat.

Al-Razi presents a simple yet profound observation: when people say 'I', they instinctively point to their chest. This universal behavior, he argues, is not arbitrary but reveals a necessary knowledge shared by all humans about the seat of the self. In this lesson, we will explore how this everyday act becomes a theological argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the brevity of the argument.
2
Identify the key claim
The passage states that everyone, when saying 'I', points to their chest. This is a universal observation. Ask yourself: is this true in your experience?
3
Understand the conclusion
Al-Razi concludes that this gesture indicates that the referent of 'I' is located in the heart. He calls this 'necessary knowledge' (al-ḍarūra).
Necessary knowledge is immediate, not derived from reasoning.
4
Reflect on the argument's nature
This is not a logical proof but an appeal to intuition and common sense. Consider why Al-Razi might consider this convincing.
Compare with other arguments that use formal logic.
5
Check your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to ensure you grasped the main point.
The question is answerable directly from the passage.

الحجة الخامسة : كل أحد إذا قال ( أنا ) فإنه يشير إلى صدره ، وإلى ناحية قلبه . وهذا يدل على أن [ كل أحد يعلم بالضرورة (۱) ] أن المشار إليه بقوله : أنا و حاصل في القلب ، لا في سائر الأعضاء
The fifth proof: Everyone, when he says 'I' (ana), points to his chest and to the direction of his heart. This indicates that [everyone knows by necessity] that that which is referred to by his saying 'I' is located in the heart, not in the other limbs.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage is the fifth argument in the series, a simple appeal to common human behavior. The author observes that whenever a person utters the word 'I' (ana), they instinctively gesture towards their chest, specifically the area of the heart. This universal and spontaneous action, the author argues, reveals a necessary knowledge (bi al-ḍarūra) that the referent of 'I' — the self or soul — is located in the heart, not in any other part of the body. The argument is not syllogistic but relies on intuition and consensus; it treats this gesture as evidence of an innate awareness shared by all people.

The Sixth Argument: Speech Originates from the Heart
Al-Razi argues speech comes from the heart; Galen objects using anatomy; answer refutes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Razi argues that speech originates from the heart, how Galen objects with anatomical evidence, and how the author's answer distinguishes between the true cause (السبب الحقيقي) and instrumental means.

Core Idea
The heart is the true cause of speech; the brain only provides the instruments.

This passage presents the sixth proof for the rational soul's location, followed by Galen's anatomical objection and the author's rebuttal. The argument hinges on distinguishing the true cause from instrumental causes. We will trace the reasoning step by step, examining each phase of the debate.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once for an overview, then read the literal translation. Note the structure: proof, objection, answer.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the main claim and structure
The author claims the heart is the source of speech. Galen objects with three anatomical arguments. The answer reinterprets them.
3
Analyze Galen's three anatomical arguments
Read each of Galen's three points: the larynx and nerves, abdominal muscle fatigue, and brain manipulation. Understand how each points to the brain as cause.
These are empirical observations.
4
Understand the author's response
The author distinguishes the true cause (heart, via breath) from instrumental causes (brain, larynx, etc.). This preserves the claim that the rational soul resides in the heart.
This logical maneuver is key.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السادسة : إن أظهر آثار النفس الناطقة هو النطق ، فوجب أن يكون معدن النفس الناطقة ، هو الموضع الذي منه تنبعث آلة النطق ، لكن آلة النطق هو الصوت ، والصوت إنما يتولد من إخراج النفس ، وإخراج النفس إنما يحصل بفعل القلب لأن القلب يستدخل النسيم الطيب للروح (۲) فإذا تسخن ذلك النسيم واحترق ، أخرجه إلى الخارج . وإذا كان إدخال النسيم وإخراجه مقصوداً للقلب ، ومصلحة له ، كان إسناد هذا الفعل إلى القلب ، أولى من إسناده إلى الدماغ، الذي لا حاجة به البتة إلى النفس .
أجاب ( جالينوس ) عن هذه الحجة : بأن الصوت لا ينبعث من القلب ، بل من الدماغ . ويدل عليه وجوه :
الأول : إن الآلة الأولى للصوت هي الحنجرة . والدليل عليه : أنك إذا خرقت (۳) قصبة الرئة أسفل من الحنجرة ، لم تسمع لهذا الحيوان صوتاً لأنك إذا فعلت بهذا الحيوان هذا الفعل ، لم يصل الهواء الخارج إلى الحنجرة بل تفرق وانتشر . وإذا لم يصل الهواء إلى الحنجرة ، وكانت الحنجرة هي الآلة للصوت . لا جرم يبطل الصوت . فثبت : أن الآلة لحدوث الصوت هي الحنجرة . والحنجرة مؤلفة من ثلاثة غضاريف ، وهذه الغضاريف إنما تتحرك [ بعضلات كثيرة ، وتلك العضلات إنما تتحرك (۱) ] بالأعصاب والأعصاب ثابتة من الدماغ . فثبت : أن فاعل الصوت هو الدماغ
والوجه الثاني في بيان أن فاعل الصوت هو الدماغ : إنا نشاهد عضل البطن يتمدد عند التصويت بالصوت العنيف . وأما القلب ، فإنه لا يناله التعب عند التصويت
•
الثالث : إن القلب إذا كشف عنه ثم قبض عليه ، فإنه لا يبطل من الحيوان صوته ، وإن كشف عن الدماغ ثم ضغط ، بطل في الحال صوت ذلك الحيوان
فثبت بهذه الوجوه الثلاثة : أن مبدأ الصوت هو الدماغ ، لا القلب . وعند هذا البيان يصير هذا الكلام حجة [ واضحة (۲) ] على صحة أن محل القوة الناطقة هو الدماغ
والجواب : إنا بينا أن سبب حدوث الصوت : خروج النفس . وبينا : أن سبب خروج النفس هو القلب ، فلزم القطع بأن السبب الحقيقي [ لحدوث الصوت (۳) ] هو القلب . وأما الوجوه التي ذكرتم ، فهي تدل على أن الدماغ محتاج إليه في حدوث الصوت، وفي تكوين آلات حدوث الصوت ، وذلك لا يقدح في قولنا
The sixth proof: Verily, the most manifest effect of the rational soul is speech (al-nuṭq). So it is necessary that the mine (ma‘din) of the rational soul be the place from which the instrument of speech emanates. But the instrument of speech is sound (al-ṣawt), and sound is only generated by the emission of breath (ikhrāj al-nafas). And the emission of breath is only obtained by the action of the heart, because the heart draws in the pleasant breeze for the spirit (al-rūḥ). When that breeze becomes hot and burns, it expels it to the outside. And if the inhalation and exhalation of the breeze are intended for the heart and are a benefit for it, then attributing this action to the heart is more appropriate than attributing it to the brain, which has no need at all of breath.
Galen (Jālīnūs) answered this proof: that sound does not emanate from the heart, but from the brain. And this is indicated by several aspects:
First: The primary instrument of sound is the larynx (al-ḥanjara). The proof of this is that if you perforate the trachea below the larynx, you will not hear a sound from that animal because the air that goes out does not reach the larynx but disperses and spreads. When the air does not reach the larynx, and the larynx is the instrument of sound, inevitably sound is nullified. So it is established that the instrument for the occurrence of sound is the larynx. The larynx is composed of three cartilages, and these cartilages are moved by many muscles, and those muscles are moved by nerves, and the nerves originate from the brain. So it is established that the agent (fā‘il) of sound is the brain.
The second aspect in explaining that the agent of sound is the brain: We observe that the abdominal muscles become extended when producing a loud sound. As for the heart, it does not experience fatigue when producing sound.
Third: If the heart is uncovered and then grasped, it does not cause the animal to lose its sound. But if the brain is uncovered and then pressed, the sound of that animal is immediately lost.
So it is established by these three aspects that the principle of sound is the brain, not the heart. And with this clarification, this discussion becomes a clear proof that the locus (maḥall) of the rational power is the brain.
The answer: We have shown that the cause of the occurrence of sound is the emission of breath. And we have shown that the cause of the emission of breath is the heart. So it is necessarily concluded that the true cause [of the occurrence of sound] is the heart. As for the aspects you mentioned, they indicate that the brain is needed in the occurrence of sound and in the formation of the instruments of sound, and that does not detract from our statement.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage is a self-contained segment comprising the sixth proof (al-hujja al-sādisa), Galen’s objection, and the author’s answer. The proof begins from the observation that speech (al-nuṭq) is the most evident effect of the rational soul. The author reasons that the mine (ma‘din) of the rational soul must be where the instrument of speech originates. That instrument is sound (al-ṣawt), which is produced by the emission of breath (ikhrāj al-nafas). Since the heart controls inhalation and exhalation, the heart is the true source of speech, not the brain, which has no need of breath.
Galen responds with three anatomical arguments: (1) the larynx is the primary instrument of sound, and its movement depends on nerves from the brain; (2) abdominal muscles—not the heart—become fatigued during loud sound; (3) direct manipulation of the brain (but not the heart) silences an animal. He concludes that the brain is the principle (mabda’) of sound and thus the locus (maḥall) of the rational power.
The author’s answer reinterprets the evidence: the heart is the true cause (al-sabab al-ḥaqīqī) of sound because it is the cause of breath emission. The brain and its structures are merely instrumental and facilitatory. Thus Galen’s aspects do not refute the claim; they only show that the brain is needed for the instrument, not for the primary causation. This distinction between essential causation and instrumental means is a key logical maneuver in Islamic theology and philosophy.

Key Terms

النطق
الصوت
النفس (الأنفاس)
القلب
الدماغ
الحنجرة
السبب الحقيقي
آلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Galen's anatomical evidence proves that the brain is the true cause of speech.
Correction: The author agrees that the brain is instrumentally necessary, but insists that the heart is the true cause because it initiates the breath that produces sound.

Key Takeaway

Eighth Proof: The Heart and Common Language
An argument from common language and a response to Galen's objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses common language as evidence for the heart being the seat of intelligence and how he refutes Galen's objection.

Core Idea
Common language reveals that the heart is the seat of intelligence, not just emotion.

The author presents his eighth proof by pointing to how people naturally speak: they say 'intelligent heart' or 'dull heart.' Galen objects that such language really refers to courage, not intelligence. The author answers that this only shows the heart is also the seat of anger, which does not negate it being the seat of understanding. This lesson guides you through this concise argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage has three distinct parts: proof, objection, response.
2
Identify the three parts
The passage contains the proof from common language, Galen's objection, and the author's response. Make sure you can distinguish each one.
3
Consider the logic
How does the author use common language as evidence? How does he distinguish between understanding and anger? Think about why Galen's objection does not defeat the proof.
The key is that the heart can be the place of both anger and understanding.

الحجة الثامنة : إن الناس يصفون القلب بالذكاء والبلادة . فيقولون : لفلان قلب ذكي ، ولفلان قلب بليد . قال جالينوس : الناس إذا وصفوا إنساناً بأن له قلباً قوياً ، فمرادهم منه الشجاعة ، وإذا قالوا : فلان لا قلب له ، فالمراد : هو الجين [؟] . والجواب : إن الذي ذكره جالينوس يدل على أن القلب مكان للغضب ، ولا يدل على أنه يمتنع أن يكون القلب موضعاً للفهم . والله أعلم.
The eighth proof: People describe the heart with intelligence and dullness. They say: So-and-so has an intelligent heart, and so-and-so has a dull heart. Galen said: When people describe a person as having a strong heart, they mean courage, and when they say: So-and-so has no heart, the meaning is: he is a coward [؟]. The answer: What Galen mentioned indicates that the heart is the place of anger, but does not indicate that it is impossible for the heart to be the place of understanding. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage presents an argument from common language and a response to an objection. The argument is that people attribute intelligence and dullness to the heart, indicating it is the seat of understanding. The objection from Galen states that people refer to a 'strong heart' for courage, not understanding. The response is that Galen's point only shows the heart is the place of anger, not that it cannot also be the place of understanding. The passage ends with 'And God knows best.'

Classification and First Proof for the Origination of Rational Souls
Al-Razi classifies opinions and gives the first proof for the soul's creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the classification of opinions on the eternity of rational souls and the first proof that demonstrates their origination.

Core Idea
The soul cannot be eternal because in pre-eternity it cannot be either one or many.

Al-Razi presents a systematic classification of possible views on whether rational souls are eternal or created, then provides a powerful argument that eliminates both unity and multiplicity in pre-eternity. This first proof is foundational in Islamic philosophical theology, showing that the soul must be originated.

Guided Path
1
Understand the classification
Read the first part of the passage where Al-Razi divides the possible positions into four: eternal (either necessary or contingent) or originated (either pre-existent to bodies or not).
Notice that this classification covers all logical possibilities.
2
Follow the proof's initial division
The proof assumes souls are eternal and then argues they must be either one or many in pre-eternity. Both alternatives are examined.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum structure.
3
Examine the refutation of oneness
If souls were one, upon attachment to bodies they would either remain one (leading to all humans sharing one soul and identical knowledge) or become multiple (which either contradicts pre-eternal oneness or implies origination).
The absurdity of shared knowledge is a strong intuitive counterexample.
4
Examine the refutation of multiplicity
If souls were many in pre-eternity, they would need a distinguishing factor by essence, necessary concomitants, or accidents. Essence and concomitants are shared, and accidents require bodies (which don't exist in pre-eternity).
This shows that multiplicity is impossible without matter.
5
Grasp the conclusion
Since both unity and multiplicity in pre-eternity are impossible, souls cannot be eternal; they must be originated.
This proof is considered decisive by those who accept its premises.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السابع في أن النفوس الناطقة محدثة أو قديمة؟ وفيه أقوال : وضبطها : أن يقال : إنها إما قديمة أو حادثة . فإن كانت قديمة فإما أن يقال إنها واجبة لذواتها غنية عن السبب والمؤثر . وإما أن يقال : إنها ممكنة لذواتها واجبة بإيجاب سببها وعلتها . وأما إن قلنا : إنها محدثة. فإما أن يقال إنها وإن كانت محدثة إلا أنها كانت موجودة قبل هذه الأبدان ، كما ورد في بعض الأخبار : ( إن الله تعالى خلق الأرواح قبل الأجساد بألفي عام )، وإما أن يقال : إن هذه الأرواح ما كانت موجودة قبل أبدانها . وهذا هو قول أرسطاطاليس وأتباعه من المتقدمين والمتأخرين. واحتج القائلون بحدوث النفس بوجهين : الحجة الأولى : هي أن قالوا : لو كانت النفوس قديمة ، لكانت في الأزل ، إما أن تكون واحدة ، أو متعددة . والقسمان باطلان ، فبطل القول بكونها قديمة . وإنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع أن يقال : إنها كانت واحدة ، لأنها لو كانت واحدة في الأزل، فعند تعلقها بالأبدان، إما أن يقال: إنها تبقى على تلك الوحدة ، وإما أن يقال : إنها عند تعلقها بالأبدان تتعدد . والقسمان باطلان . أما الأول : فلان على هذا التقدير، يلزم أن يكون الحاصل لجميع أشخاص الناس : نفساً واحدة بالعدد . ولو كان الأمر كذلك ، لكان ما علمه إنسان ، فقد علمه كل إنسان ، وما جهله إنسان فقد جهله كل إنسان . ومعلوم أنه باطل . وأما الثاني : وهو أن يقال : النفوس كانت واحدة قبل تعلقها بالأبدان . ثم إنها عند تعلقها بالأبدان : صارت متعددة. فهذا محال . لأن هاتين النفسين المتشخصتين . إما أن يقال : إنهما كانتا موجودتين في الأزل أو ما كانتا موجودتين في الأزل . فإن كانتا موجودتين في الأزل ، فقد كان التعدد حاصلاً في الأزل وقد فرضنا أنه ما كان حاصلا . هذا خلف . وإن قلنا : إنهما ما كانتا موجودتين في الأزل ، كان وجودهما حاصلاً بعد العدم . وهذا يوجب القول بحدوثهما ، ويمنع من القول بقدمهما وهو المطلوب . وإنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع القول بأنها كانت متعددة في الأزل ، لأن التعدد لا يحصل إلا إذا امتازت كل واحدة منها عن الأخرى في أمر من الأمور . وذلك الامتياز إما أن يكون حاصلا بالماهية أو بلوازمها أو بعوارضها . والأول باطل . لأنه ثبت أن النفوس الناطقة البشرية متساوية في الماهية. وإن نازع منازع في هذه المقدمة ، إلا أنه لا أقل من أن توجد نفسان متساويتان في الماهية. وهذا القدر يكفينا في تقرير هذا الدليل . والثاني أيضاً باطل . لأن لوازم الماهية مشترك فيها بين أفراد الماهية . والوصف المشترك فيه يمتنع أن يفيد الامتياز . والثالث أيضاً باطل . لأن اختلاف الأمثال بسبب العوارض المفارقة، لا يحصل إلا بسبب التغاير في المادة . ومواد النفوس هي الأبدان فقبل حصول الأبدان كانت المواد مفقودة ، فوجب أن يمتنع حصول التغاير بينها بسبب الأعراض المفارقة . فثبت : حصولها في الأزل على نعت الوحدة محال وعلى نعت التعدد أيضاً : محال . فوجب القطع بأنه يمتنع حصولها في الأزل.
The seventh [section] concerning whether rational souls are originated or eternal? And concerning it there are opinions: and their summary is that it is said: they are either eternal or originated. If they are eternal, then either it is said that they are necessary in themselves, independent of cause and effect; or it is said that they are possible in themselves, necessary by the necessitation of their cause and ground. And if we say they are originated, then either it is said that although they are originated, they existed before these bodies, as is reported in some traditions: 'God most high created the spirits two thousand years before the bodies'; or it is said that these spirits did not exist before their bodies. And this is the opinion of Aristotle and his followers among the ancients and moderns. And those who hold the origination of the soul argued with two proofs: The first proof is that they said: If souls were eternal, then in pre-eternity they would be either one or many. Both divisions are false, so the statement that they are eternal is false. And we say: It is impossible to say that they were one, because if they were one in pre-eternity, then upon their attachment to bodies, either it is said that they remain on that unity, or it is said that upon their attachment to bodies they become multiple. Both divisions are false. As for the first: because on this supposition, it would follow that what results for all individual people is numerically one soul. And if it were so, then what one human knows, every human would know, and what one human is ignorant of, every human would be ignorant of. And it is known that this is false. As for the second: which is to say: the souls were one before their attachment to bodies, then upon attachment to bodies they become multiple. This is impossible. Because those two individuated souls: either it is said that they both existed in pre-eternity or they did not exist in pre-eternity. If they existed in pre-eternity, then multiplicity would have occurred in pre-eternity, but we had assumed it did not occur. This is a contradiction. And if we say they did not exist in pre-eternity, their existence occurred after non-existence. This necessitates the statement of their origination and prevents the statement of their eternity, which is what is sought. And we say: It is impossible to say that they were multiple in pre-eternity, because multiplicity does not occur unless each one of them is distinguished from the other in some respect. That distinction is either by essence or by its necessary concomitants or by its accidents. The first is false, because it is established that human rational souls are equal in essence. And if someone disputes this premise, then at the very least it is possible that two souls exist equal in essence, and this suffices for our presentation of this proof. The second is also false, because the necessary concomitants of the essence are shared among individuals of the essence, and a shared attribute cannot produce distinction. The third is also false, because differentiation of similar things by separable accidents only occurs due to variation in matter, and the matters of souls are bodies. So before the existence of bodies, matters were non-existent, so it must be impossible for variation among them to occur due to separable accidents. Thus it is established: their existence in pre-eternity in the mode of unity is impossible, and in the mode of multiplicity is also impossible. Therefore it is necessarily concluded that their existence in pre-eternity is impossible.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage presents a classification of opinions on the question of whether rational souls (al-nufus al-natiqa) are eternal (qadima) or originated (haditha) and then gives the first proof of those who hold origination. The author first divides the possible positions: souls are either eternal or originated. If eternal, they are either necessary in themselves or contingent but necessitated by a cause. If originated, they either existed before bodies (as some traditions suggest) or did not (the view of Aristotle and his followers). Then he presents the first proof: if souls were eternal, they would in pre-eternity (al-azal) be either one or many. Both options are impossible. If they were one, then upon attachment to bodies they would either remain one or become multiple. If they remain one, then all humans would share one soul, leading to identical knowledge and ignorance—absurd. If they become multiple after being one, then the newly multiple souls must either have existed in pre-eternity (contradicting the assumption of oneness) or come into existence after non-existence, which implies origination—the desired conclusion. Next, the author argues that multiplicity in pre-eternity is also impossible because distinction requires a distinguishing factor—either essence, necessary concomitants, or accidents. Essence cannot distinguish because souls are equal in essence. Concomitants are shared and cannot differentiate. Accidents require matter (bodies), which do not exist in pre-eternity. Therefore, souls cannot be multiple in pre-eternity. Since both unity and multiplicity are impossible, souls cannot be eternal; they must be originated.

Key Terms
النفوس الناطقة
الأزل
الوحدة
التعدد
الماهية
اللوازم
العوارض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the argument only disproves the oneness of souls but leaves open the possibility of multiplicity.
Correction: Al-Razi explicitly argues that multiplicity is also impossible because distinction requires a factor that cannot exist in pre-eternity (shared essence/concomitants, or accidents requiring bodies).

Checkpoint
According to the first proof, if the souls were one in pre-eternity and remained one when attached to bodies, what would be the consequence?
A) All humans would have distinct knowledge.
B) All humans would have the same knowledge and ignorance.
C) Souls would become multiple.
D) The soul would cease to exist.

Key Takeaway
The first proof shows that souls cannot be eternal because both unity and multiplicity in pre-eternity lead to logical absurdities, thus they must be originated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your rational soul is not self-sufficient but created and contingent, how does that challenge your tendency to act as if you are independent of God? Will you spend a few minutes today meditating on your absolute need for His continued existence?
?
The proof shows that the soul cannot be eternal because it would lead to logical contradictions. Is there any area of your life where you are living as if your soul is independent of its Creator, ignoring the clear proofs of its dependence? What concrete step can you take today to realign your life with the truth of your createdness?
?
Al-Razi argues that the soul's existence is impossible both as one and as many in pre-eternity. How does this logical conclusion affect your view of your own uniqueness? Does it make you realize that your distinct personhood is a gift from God, created at a specific moment, not an eternal given? How can you express gratitude for this gift today?

beginner

Souls Cannot Be One in Number
A reductio ad absurdum against the numerical unity of souls.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why souls cannot be a single numerical entity, based on the absurd consequence of universal knowledge.

Core Idea
If all souls were one, everyone would know the same things — which is false.

The author begins his proof that souls are not pre-eternal by eliminating the possibility that they are one in number. He presents a simple reductio ad absurdum: if all souls were identical, then knowledge would be universal. Since this is clearly not the case, souls cannot be a single entity. This foundational argument sets the stage for further reasoning about multiplicity and pre-eternity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation, noticing the conditional structure: if souls were one, then...
2
Understand the consequence
The author argues that if souls were one, then knowledge would be universal — everyone would know everything. Why is that a consequence of numerical unity?
If all souls are identical, then whatever one knows, all know.
3
Recognize the refutation
The author states that this consequence is 'known to be false' (bāṭil). This refutes the assumption that souls are one in number.
The falsity is obvious from our experience.
4
Connect to the larger argument
This is just the first step. In later lessons, we will see that souls cannot be many in pre-eternity either.

Source Text

The individuals of people are one soul in number. And if it were so, then whatever a human knows, every human would know it, and whatever a human is ignorant of, every human would be ignorant of it. And it is known that this is false. As for the second: that it is said: souls were one before their attachment to bodies. Then when they attach to bodies, they become multiple. This is impossible. For these two particular souls: either it is said that they both existed in pre-eternity, or they did not exist in pre-eternity. If they existed in pre-eternity, then multiplicity existed in pre-eternity, and we have assumed that it did not exist. This is a contradiction. And if we say that they did not exist in pre-eternity, then their existence occurs after non-existence. This necessitates saying that they are originated, and prevents saying they are eternal - which is what is desired. And we say: it is impossible to say that they were multiple in pre-eternity, because multiplicity does not occur unless each one is distinguished from the other by some matter. That distinction is either by essence or its necessary concomitants or its accidents. The first is false because it is established that human rational souls are equal in essence. Even if someone disputes this premise, at least there exist two souls equal in essence. And this suffices for establishing this proof. The second is also false because the necessary concomitants of the essence are shared among individuals of the essence, and a shared description cannot bring about distinction. The third is also false because the difference of instances due to separable accidents does not occur except due to variation in matter. The materials of souls are bodies, so before the existence of bodies, materials were absent, so it must be impossible for variation among them to occur due to separable accidents. Thus it is established: their existence in pre-eternity as one is impossible, and as multiple is also impossible. Therefore it must be decisively concluded that their existence in pre-eternity is impossible.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage is a proof that souls cannot be pre-eternal. The author begins by refuting the idea that all souls are numerically one. If they were one, then knowledge would be universal—everyone would know the same things—which is obviously false. Then he addresses the second claim: that souls were one in pre-eternity but became multiple upon attachment to bodies. He argues that this is impossible by considering two specific souls. If they existed in pre-eternity, multiplicity already existed, contradicting the claim that they were one. If they did not exist, then they are originated (hadith) and not eternal, which is exactly what he wants to prove. Then he adds a deeper argument: multiplicity requires distinction, and distinction must be by essence, necessary concomitants, or accidents. Essence is shared among all souls, so it cannot differentiate. Necessary concomitants are also shared. Accidents require matter, which is absent before bodies exist. Therefore, neither unity nor multiplicity in pre-eternity is possible. The conclusion is decisive: souls cannot be pre-eternal.

عدد (number)

Souls cannot be a single numerical entity because that would imply universal knowledge, which is false.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This argument shows that your soul is unique in its knowledge. You know things that no one else knows. Have you been content to keep that knowledge to yourself? What would it mean to truly accept that if you don't teach, that knowledge is lost to humanity?
?
If all souls were one, you would not need to struggle to learn or teach. But because souls are distinct, you have a personal responsibility to seek truth and share it. Are you acting as if your soul's knowledge matters? What will you do today to fulfill that responsibility?

The Dilemma of Souls Becoming Many After Unity
A dilemma refuting the claim that souls were one then became many.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second argument against pre-eternal souls: that the idea of souls being one in pre-eternity and then becoming multiple is self-contradictory.

Core Idea
Souls cannot be one and then become many; either multiplicity existed in pre-eternity or souls are created.

After refuting the idea that souls are numerically one, the author considers a second proposal: that souls were one in pre-eternity but became multiple upon attachment to bodies. He shows this is impossible through a dilemma: either the two souls existed in pre-eternity or they did not. Both options lead to problems. This argument is crucial because it forces the conclusion that souls are originated.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation, focusing on the dilemma structure.
2
Identify the two options
The author presents two possibilities: either the two souls existed in pre-eternity or they did not. Consider each.
The souls in question are two specific souls that supposedly become multiple.
3
Analyze the first option
If they existed in pre-eternity, then multiplicity existed in pre-eternity, contradicting the claim that they were one.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
4
Analyze the second option
If they did not exist in pre-eternity, then they came into existence after non-existence, meaning they are originated (ḥādith), not eternal. This is exactly what the author wants to prove.
5
Draw the conclusion
Since both options lead to the rejection of the claim that souls are pre-eternal, the claim is false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The individuals of people are one soul in number. And if it were so, then whatever a human knows, every human would know it, and whatever a human is ignorant of, every human would be ignorant of it. And it is known that this is false. As for the second: that it is said: souls were one before their attachment to bodies. Then when they attach to bodies, they become multiple. This is impossible. For these two particular souls: either it is said that they both existed in pre-eternity, or they did not exist in pre-eternity. If they existed in pre-eternity, then multiplicity existed in pre-eternity, and we have assumed that it did not exist. This is a contradiction. And if we say that they did not exist in pre-eternity, then their existence occurs after non-existence. This necessitates saying that they are originated, and prevents saying they are eternal - which is what is desired. And we say: it is impossible to say that they were multiple in pre-eternity, because multiplicity does not occur unless each one is distinguished from the other by some matter. That distinction is either by essence or its necessary concomitants or its accidents. The first is false because it is established that human rational souls are equal in essence. Even if someone disputes this premise, at least there exist two souls equal in essence. And this suffices for establishing this proof. The second is also false because the necessary concomitants of the essence are shared among individuals of the essence, and a shared description cannot bring about distinction. This passage is a proof that souls cannot be pre-eternal. The author begins by refuting the idea that all souls are numerically one. ?

?

Souls Cannot Be Multiple in Pre-Eternity Due to Lack of Distinction
A trilemma showing that distinctions necessary for multiplicity are impossible for pre-eternal souls.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the deeper argument that souls cannot be multiple in pre-eternity because distinction requires essence, concomitants, or accidents — all of which fail before bodies exist.

Core Idea
Multiplicity requires distinction, but pre-eternal souls lack the means to be distinct.

The author now provides a more fundamental analysis of why souls cannot be multiple in pre-eternity. He argues that multiplicity requires each soul to be distinguished from others. Distinction can only come from essence, necessary concomitants, or accidents. He systematically shows each is impossible for souls in pre-eternity. This rigorous argument clinches the conclusion that souls cannot be pre-eternal at all.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the tripartite classification of distinction: essence, concomitants, accidents.
2
Examine the first option (essence)
The author says essence is the same for all human souls, so it cannot distinguish them. He even allows that at least two souls are equal in essence.
This is a key premise: souls share the same essence.
3
Examine the second option (concomitants)
Necessary concomitants (lawaazim al-mahiyya) are also shared among individuals of the same essence, so they cannot provide distinction.
A shared description cannot cause difference.
4
Examine the third option (accidents)
Accidents (a'raad) can distinguish, but they require a material substrate. The materials of souls are bodies, which do not exist in pre-eternity. So no accidents possible.
Without bodies, souls cannot have separable accidents.
5
Conclude
Since all possible sources of distinction are impossible, multiplicity in pre-eternity is impossible. Combined with the earlier proof that unity is also impossible, the only conclusion is that souls are not pre-eternal.
Thus the argument is complete.

أشخاص الناس : نفساً واحدة بالعدد . ولو كان الأمر كذلك ، لكان ما علمه إنسان ، فقد علمه كل إنسان ، وما جهله إنسان فقد جهله كل إنسان . ومعلوم أنه باطل وأما الثاني : وهو أن يقال : النفوس كانت واحدة قبل تعلقها بالأبدان . ثم إنها عند تعلقها بالأبدان : صارت متعددة. فهذا محال . لأن هاتين النفسين المتشخصتين . إما أن يقال : إنهما كانتا موجودتين في الأزل أو ما كانت موجودتين في الأزل . فإن كانتا موجودتين في الأزل ، فقد كان التعدد حاصلاً في الأزل وقد فرضنا أنه ما كان حاصلا . هذا خلف . وإن قلنا : إنهما ما كانتا موجودتين في الأزل ، كان وجودهما حاصلاً بعد العدم . وهذا يوجب القول بحدوثهما ، ويمنع من القول بقدمهما وهو المطلوب . وإنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع القول بأنها كانت متعددة في الأزل ، لأن التعدد لا يحصل إلا إذا امتازت كل واحدة منها عن الأخرى في أمر من الأمور . وذلك الامتياز إما أن يكون حاصلا بالماهية أو بلوازمها أو بعوارضها . والأول باطل . لأنه ثبت أن النفوس الناطقة البشرية متساوية في الماهية. وإن نازع منازع في هذه المقدمة ، إلا أنه لا أقل من أن توجد نفسان متساويتان في الماهية. وهذا القدر يكفينا في تقرير هذا الدليل . والثاني أيضاً باطل . لأن لوازم الماهية مشترك فيها بين أفراد الماهية . والوصف المشترك فيه يمتنع أن يفيد الامتياز . والثالث أيضاً باطل . لأن اختلاف الأمثال بسبب العوارض المفارقة، لا يحصل إلا بسبب التغاير في المادة . ومواد النفوس هي الأبدان فقبل حصول الأبدان كانت المواد مفقودة ، فوجب أن يمتنع حصول التغاير بينها بسبب الأعراض المفارقة . فثبت : حصولها في الأزل على نعت الوحدة محال وعلى نعت التعدد أيضاً : محال . فوجب القطع بأنه يمتنع حصولها في الأزل
The individuals of people are one soul in number. And if it were so, then whatever a human knows, every human would know it, and whatever a human is ignorant of, every human would be ignorant of it. And it is known that this is false. As for the second: that it is said: souls were one before their attachment to bodies. Then when they attach to bodies, they become multiple. This is impossible. For these two particular souls: either it is said that they both existed in pre-eternity, or they did not exist in pre-eternity. If they existed in pre-eternity, then multiplicity existed in pre-eternity, and we have assumed that it did not exist. This is a contradiction. And if we say that they did not exist in pre-eternity, then their existence occurs after non-existence. This necessitates saying that they are originated, and prevents saying they are eternal - which is what is desired. And we say: it is impossible to say that they were multiple in pre-eternity, because multiplicity does not occur unless each one is distinguished from the other by some matter. That distinction is either by essence or its necessary concomitants or its accidents. The first is false because it is established that human rational souls are equal in essence. Even if someone disputes this premise, at least there exist two souls equal in essence. And this suffices for establishing this proof. The second is also false because the necessary concomitants of the essence are shared among individuals of the essence, and a shared description cannot bring about distinction. The third is also false because the difference of instances due to separable accidents does not occur except due to variation in matter. The materials of souls are bodies, so before the existence of bodies, materials were absent, so it must be impossible for variation among them to occur due to separable accidents. Thus it is established: their existence in pre-eternity as one is impossible, and as multiple is also impossible. Therefore it must be decisively concluded that their existence in pre-eternity is impossible.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage is a proof that souls cannot be pre-eternal. The author begins by refuting the idea that all souls are numerically one. If they were one, then knowledge would be universal—everyone would know the same things—which is obviously false. Then he addresses the second claim: that souls were one in pre-eternity but became multiple upon attachment to bodies. He argues that this is impossible by considering two specific souls. If they existed in pre-eternity, multiplicity already existed, contradicting the claim that they were one. If they did not exist, then they are originated (hadith) and not eternal, which is exactly what he wants to prove. Then he adds a deeper argument: multiplicity requires distinction, and distinction must be by essence, necessary concomitants, or accidents. Essence is shared among all souls, so it cannot differentiate. Necessary concomitants are also shared. Accidents require matter, which is absent before bodies exist. Therefore, neither unity nor multiplicity in pre-eternity is possible. The conclusion is decisive: souls cannot be pre-eternal.

Key Terms
امتياز (distinction)
ماهية (essence)
لازم (necessary concomitant)
عوارض (accidents)
مادة (matter)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think souls could be distinguished by individual essence or necessary concomitants.
Correction: Souls share the same essence, so neither essence nor its necessary concomitants can individuate them; accidents require matter which is absent before bodies.

Checkpoint
Why does the author reject distinction by accidents for pre-eternal souls?
A) Accidents are not real.
B) Accidents require matter, which is absent before bodies.
C) Accidents are shared among all souls.
D) Accidents are not allowed in kalam.

Key Takeaway
Souls cannot be multiple in pre-eternity because no basis for distinction exists before bodies.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your soul is not eternal but created by Allah, how does that reality change the way you view your fleeting moments in this life? What is one thing you will do today to honor the gift of your soul's existence?
?
The argument shows that without a body, your soul would have no individuality. How does this deepen your appreciation for your body as an essential part of your identity and worship? Are you treating your body as the trust that it is?
?
If pre-eternal multiplicity is impossible, then your soul is uniquely brought into existence at a specific moment. Does that thought make you feel more accountable to the One who gave it? What will you change to live in awareness of that accountability?

Objection and Answer on Souls Becoming Multiple After Unity
The author responds to the objection that souls were one in pre-eternity and later became multiple.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the objection that souls become multiple after unity, using a logical dilemma and a critique of universal propositions.

Core Idea
The opponent's argument against souls applies equally to bodies—yet they reject it.

In this passage, an objector challenges the idea that souls were one in pre-eternity, asking why they cannot become multiple when attached to bodies. The author responds with a two-pronged argument: first, the same logic applied to water leads to contradictions for the opponent; second, the claim that only bodies can divide after unity is an unproven universal statement. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this elegant refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to get a sense of the argument's flow.
Notice the structure: objection, first response (water dilemma), second response (conversion critique).
2
Understand the water dilemma
The author presents a dilemma: either the two waters existed before division (implying the original was composite) or they didn't (implying annihilation). Both options contradict the opponent's view of simple bodies.
3
See the parallel to the soul
The same dilemma the opponent uses against souls is now applied to bodies. Since the opponent accepts bodies divide but rejects the dilemma for them, his position is inconsistent.
4
Examine the second objection
The opponent then claims that only bodies can divide after being one. The author shows that this universal affirmative proposition does not convert; it is not proven that non-bodies cannot also have this property.
5
Reflect on the overall refutation
Ask yourself: Why is this refutation effective? It shows that the opponent's own principles lead to absurdities, and the alternative argument is unsubstantiated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأول : أن نقول : لم لا يجوز أن يقال : إنها في الأزل كانت واحدة ، ثم صارت عند التعلق بالأبدان متعددة ؟ قوله : ( هاتان النفسان المعينتان . إما أن يقال : إنهما كانتا موجودتين في الأزل ، أو ما كانتا موجودتين في الأزل ، قلنا : هذا الدليل جيد في نفسه ، إلا أنه لا يستقيم على أصولكم ، وذلك لأنكم تقولون : إن هذا الماء ، كان واحداً في ذاته ، وعند القسمة يحصل ماءان . فيقال لكم هذان الماءان . هل كانا موجودين قبل حصول هذه القسمة ، أو ما كانا موجودين ؟ فإن كان الأول فذلك الماء . قبل هذه القسمة ما كان ماءاً واحداً في ذاته ، بل كان مركباً مؤلفاً من الأجزاء . وحينئذ يبطل قولكم إن الجسم البسيط واحد من نفسه . وإن قلتم : إن هذين الماءين الحاصلين بعد القسمة ، ما كانا موجودين من قبل القسمة ، فيلزم أن يقال : إن هذين الماءين حدثا الآن ، وذلك الماء الذي كان واحداً قبل القسمة ، فيلزم أن يقال : إن هذين الماءين حدثا الآن ، وذلك الماء الذي كان واحداً قبل القسمة : قد فني وعدم عند حصول هذه القسمة . فيكون التقسيم إعداماً للماء الأول ، وإيجاداً للماء الثاني . وذلك لا يقوله عاقل . فثبت بهذا : أن الدليل الذي ذكرتم في امتناع أن تتعدد النفوس بعد وحدتها : قائم بعينه في الأجسام . مع أنكم لا تقولون به ، فكان الإلزام وارداً . فإن قالوا : نحن لا نذكر في إبطال هذا القسم : هذا الدليل الذي ذكرتم . بل تذكر كلاماً آخر ، وهو أن نقول : كل ما انقسم بعد أن كان واحداً ، فهو جسم . ونحن قد بينا : أن النفس ليست بجسم . فنقول : هذا الكلام ضعيف . لأنه يصدق أن يكون الجسم واحداً ، ثم يتعدد . ولا يلزم من صدقه أن كل ما كان واحداً ثم تعدد ، فإنه يكون جسماً لان الموجبة الكلية لا تنعكس مثل نفسها ، فلعله يكون الجسم بهذه الصفة . وغير الجسم قد يكون أيضاً بهذه الصفة . فيما لم تذكروا الدليل لم يتم هذا الكلام
First: that we say: Why is it not permissible to say that they were one in pre-eternity, then when attached to bodies they become multiple? He said: (These two specific souls: either it is said that they both existed in pre-eternity, or they did not exist in pre-eternity). We say: This proof is good in itself, but it is not valid according to your principles, because you say that this water was one in itself, and upon division two waters come into existence. So it is said to you: Were these two waters existing before this division, or were they not existing? If the first, then that water before this division was not one in itself, but rather composed of parts. And then your statement that a simple body is one in itself is invalidated. And if you say that these two waters that arise after division were not existing before the division, then it follows that these two waters came into existence now, and that water that was one before division has perished and become non-existent at the occurrence of this division. So division becomes a destruction of the first water and a creation of the second water. And no rational person would say that. So it is established by this: that the proof you mentioned against the possibility of souls becoming multiple after their unity is equally applicable to bodies, even though you do not accept it. So the objection is valid. Then if they say: We do not mention this proof you mentioned in refuting this type. Rather we mention another statement, which is that we say: Everything that divides after being one is a body. And we have shown that the soul is not a body. We say: This statement is weak. For it is true that a body can be one and then become multiple. But it does not follow from its truth that everything that was one and then becomes multiple is a body, because the universal affirmative proposition does not convert as itself. Perhaps the body has this characteristic, and other than body may also have this characteristic. As long as you have not provided the proof, this statement is not established.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage is an objection and answer. The objector asks: Why can't souls be one in pre-eternity and then become multiple when attached to bodies? The author responds by showing that the same logic applies to bodies, which the opponent considers simple and one. Using the example of water, the author points out a dilemma: either the two waters existed before division (implying the original water was composite, contradicting its simplicity) or they did not (implying the original water was annihilated and new waters created, which is absurd). Thus, the argument against souls becoming multiple holds equally for bodies, but the opponent rejects it for bodies, exposing inconsistency. Then the opponent tries a different argument: only bodies can divide after being one, and since the soul is not a body, it cannot divide. The author counters that this claim is weak because just because bodies have this property does not mean only bodies have it. The universal statement is not proven; it could be that non-bodies also divide. Without proof, the objection fails.

Key Terms
نفس (soul)
جسم (body)
قسمة (division)
أصل (principle)
إلزام (objection)
موجبة كلية (universal affirmative)
انعكاس (conversion)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the proof against souls becoming multiple is invalid because souls are not bodies, so the opponent's argument about division only applying to bodies is sound.
Correction: The author shows that the same argument used against souls also applies to bodies on the opponent's own principles, and the claim that only bodies divide is an unproven universal statement that does not convert.

Checkpoint
What does the author use to refute the objection that souls could become multiple after unity?
A) A proof that bodies cannot divide.
B) The same argument applied to water and bodies.
C) An appeal to revelation.
D) A claim that souls are eternal.

Key Takeaway
The author refutes the objection by showing that the opponent's own logic about bodies leads to absurdities, and the claim that only bodies divide is unproven.

Where in your life have you demanded proof from others while ignoring the same flaws in your own beliefs? Take a moment to identify one such area and commit to examining it honestly.
?
The opponent shifts arguments when cornered. Have you ever changed your reasoning mid-debate to avoid a difficult conclusion? This lesson demands intellectual consistency. What is one area in your faith practice where you need to be more consistent, even if it is uncomfortable?
?

Think of a situation where your actions contradict your stated principles. How will you resolve that tension today?

Turning the Tables: The Water Analogy and the Soul's Unity
First objection and response using water analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the objector's own argument against the soul's multiplicity is shown to apply equally to bodies, and how the rebuttal uses logical principles like the conversion of universal affirmatives.

Core Idea
The objector's proof against soul multiplicity works equally against bodies—yet they do not accept it.

This passage presents a classic dialectical move in kalam: turning an opponent's argument back against them. The objector argues that souls cannot be multiple after being one in pre-eternity, but the responder shows that the same logic would apply to bodies, which the objector does not accept. Then a second objection based on 'dividing after being one implies body' is rebutted using logical conversion.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
First, read the objector's claim that souls could be one in pre-eternity and then become multiple. Then note the responder's initial comment that the objector's own proof is good in itself but not sound according to their principles.
Pay attention to the shift from the objector's argument to the water analogy.
2
Analyze the water analogy dilemma
The responder presents a dilemma: either the two waters existed before division or not. Examine each horn and its consequences. Understand why both lead to unacceptable conclusions for the objector.
This is the core of the dialectical move.
3
Observe the conclusion for bodies
The responder concludes that the same proof used against souls applies exactly to bodies, yet the objector does not accept it for bodies. This shows the objection is valid.
The responder uses this to show inconsistency.
4
Examine the second objection and rebuttal
The objector tries a different argument: all that divides after being one is a body, and the soul is not a body. The responder rebuts using logic: universal affirmative statements do not convert simply.
This demonstrates the importance of logical form in kalam arguments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأول : أن نقول : لم لا يجوز أن يقال : إنها في الأزل كانت واحدة ، ثم صارت عند التعلق بالأبدان متعددة ؟ قوله : ( هاتان النفسان المعينتان . إما أن يقال : إنهما كانتا موجودتين في الأزل ، أو ما كانتا موجودتين في الأزل ، قلنا : هذا الدليل جيد في نفسه ، إلا أنه لا يستقيم على أصولكم ، وذلك لأنكم تقولون : إن هذا الماء ، كان واحداً في ذاته ، وعند القسمة يحصل ماءان . فيقال لكم هذان الماءان . هل كانا موجودين قبل حصول هذه القسمة ، أو ما كانا موجودين ؟ فإن كان الأول فذلك الماء . قبل هذه القسمة ما كان ماءاً واحداً في ذاته ، بل كان مركباً مؤلفاً من الأجزاء . وحينئذ يبطل قولكم إن الجسم البسيط واحد من نفسه . وإن قلتم : إن هذين الماءين الحاصلين بعد القسمة ، ما كانا موجودين من قبل القسمة ، فيلزم أن يقال : إن هذين الماءين حدثا الآن ، وذلك الماء الذي كان واحداً قبل القسمة ، فيلزم أن يقال : إن هذين الماءين حدثا الآن ، وذلك الماء الذي كان واحداً قبل القسمة : قد فني وعدم عند حصول هذه القسمة . فيكون التقسيم إعداماً للماء الأول ، وإيجاداً للماء الثاني . وذلك لا يقوله عاقل . فثبت بهذا : أن الدليل الذي ذكرتم في امتناع أن تتعدد النفوس بعد وحدتها : قائم بعينه في الأجسام . مع أنكم لا تقولون به ، فكان الإلزام وارداً . فإن قالوا : نحن لا نذكر في إبطال هذا القسم : هذا الدليل الذي ذكرتم . بل تذكر كلاماً آخر ، وهو أن نقول : كل ما انقسم بعد أن كان واحداً ، فهو جسم . ونحن قد بينا : أن النفس ليست بجسم . فنقول : هذا الكلام ضعيف . لأنه يصدق أن يكون الجسم واحداً ، ثم يتعدد . ولا يلزم من صدقه أن كل ما كان واحداً ثم تعدد ، فإنه يكون جسماً لان الموجبة الكلية لا تنعكس مثل نفسها ، فلعله يكون الجسم بهذه الصفة . وغير الجسم قد يكون أيضاً بهذه الصفة . فيما لم تذكروا الدليل لم يتم هذا الكلام
The first: that we say: why is it not permissible to say that they (souls) were one in pre-eternity, then became multiple when attached to bodies? His statement: 'These two particular souls, either it is said that they existed in pre-eternity, or they did not exist in pre-eternity.' We said: This proof is good in itself, but it is not sound according to your principles. That is because you say: This water was one in its essence, and upon division two waters occur. So it is said to you: These two waters — were they existing before this division occurred, or were they not existing? If the first, then that water before this division was not one in its essence, but rather was composed and made up of parts. And then your statement that the simple body is one from itself is invalidated. And if you say: These two waters occurring after division were not existing before the division, then it follows that these two waters have come into existence now, and that water which was one before the division — it follows that these two waters have come into existence now, and that water which was one before the division has perished and become non-existent upon the occurrence of this division. So division becomes an annihilation of the first water and a bringing into existence of the second water. And no rational person says that. So it is established by this that the proof you mentioned for the impossibility of souls becoming multiple after their unity is exactly applicable to bodies. Yet you do not say it, so the objection is valid. If they say: We do not mention in refuting this section the proof you mentioned, but rather we mention another statement, which is that we say: Everything that divides after being one is a body, and we have shown that the soul is not a body. We say: This statement is weak; because it is true that the body can be one and then become multiple, but it does not follow from its truth that everything that was one and then becomes multiple is a body — because the universal affirmative does not convert as itself (simple conversion). So perhaps the body has this attribute, and other than the body may also have this attribute. Since you have not mentioned the proof, this statement is not complete.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage presents a first objection and its response in a debate about the soul's unity and multiplicity. The objection asks: Why can't it be said that souls were one in pre-eternity and only became multiple when attached to bodies? The responder begins by noting that the objector's own proof (about two particular souls either existing or not existing in pre-eternity) is good in itself but does not hold up according to the objector's own principles. He illustrates this with an analogy: materialists hold that water is one in essence, but upon division it becomes two waters. The responder then poses a dilemma: either the two waters existed before the division or they did not. If they existed, then the original water was not truly one but composed of parts, invalidating the claim that a simple body is one from itself. If they did not exist, then the two waters are new, and the original water perishes, implying division annihilates and creates. This, he says, no rational person would accept. Thus the very proof used against the soul applies equally to bodies, which materialists do not accept, so the objection is valid. The objector then tries a different argument: everything that divides after being one is a body, and the soul is not a body. The responder counters that this is weak because the universal affirmative (all that divides are bodies) does not convert; it does not imply that all that are one and then multiple are bodies—bodies happen to have that property, but non-bodies might as well. Since the objector hasn't provided a proof, the argument remains incomplete.

Key Terms
نفس (soul)
أزل (pre-eternity)
تعدد (multiplicity)
جسم (body)
انقسام (division)
موجبة كلية (universal affirmative)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The water analogy is meant to prove that the soul can be multiple after being one.
Correction: The water analogy is used to show a flaw in the objector's own reasoning by applying the same logic to bodies, not to prove the soul's multiplicity.

Checkpoint
What does the responder conclude about the proof that the soul cannot become multiple after being one?
A) It is entirely false.
B) It applies equally to bodies, but the objector does not accept it.
C) It only works if the soul is a body.
D) It is valid but requires further proof.

Key Takeaway
The objector's own argument can be turned against them using a simple analogy and logical consistency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just read how an objector was caught by his own logic. When you debate your beliefs, do you hold your opponent to standards you yourself violate? Where in your life are you inconsistent in your reasoning about the soul? Will you examine your own assumptions today?
?
The objector tried to escape by shifting the argument. When God's signs confront your comfortable worldview, do you evade instead of submitting? What would it cost you to sincerely submit to the truth, even if it uproots your pride?
?
Think of a time you used an argument that could easily be turned against you. How did it feel? This lesson shows that logical consistency matters before God. Will you commit to being honest with yourself and others, even when it exposes your flaws?

The First Proof: Infinite Regress of Individualities
First argument against the second objection: infinite regress.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first refutation: that if individuality were an added attribute, it would lead to infinite regress, and that combining universals cannot yield particularity.

Core Idea
If individuality is added, each individuality needs another, leading to an endless chain.

The first argument against the second objection tackles the idea that determinate individuality (ta'ayyun) could be an additional attribute to the essence. The objector claimed that multiplicity requires a distinct meaning. The responder here shows that if that meaning is itself an added attribute, then each such attribute would require yet another attribute, ad infinitum. This lesson unpacks that logical problem and a potential counterargument.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the first argument segment in Arabic. Notice how it begins with 'إنه لو كان التعين أمراً زائداً' and the structure of the conditional.
The argument uses a conditional to show the consequence.
2
Identify the core claim
The passage asserts that if ta'ayyun were additional, then each ta'ayyun would require another ta'ayyun, leading to infinite regress.
Note the term 'تسلسل' (infinite regress).
3
Examine the counterargument
The objector proposes that quiddities like blackness and individuality could mutually necessitate each other. Read how the responder rejects this by pointing out that both are universals.
A universal combined with a universal remains universal.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The proof ends by stating that the objector's suggestion does not necessitate individuality. Consider why this refutes the objection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاعتراض الثاني : لم لا يجوز أن يقال : النفوس كانت متعددة في الأزل ؟ قوله : « إنه لا يحصل التعدد إلا لأجل معنى يوجب الإمتياز ، قلنا : هذا ممنوع . ويدل عليه وجوه : الأول : إنه لو كان التعين أمراً زائداً على الذات والتعينات متساوية في ماهية أنها تعين ، وجب أن يكون تعين كل تعين زائداً عليه . ويلزم التسلسل . ولا يقال : لم لا يجوز أن يقال : ماهية السواد، وماهية التعين ، إذا انضمت كل واحدة منهما إلى الأخرى ، فإن كل واحدة منهما تقتضي تعين الأخرى ؟ لأنـا نقول : ماهية السواد ماهية كلية ، وماهية التعين أيضاً ماهية كلية ، والكل إذا تقيد بالكلي يبقى كلياً ، ولا يصير شخصياً . فثبت : أن القدر الذي ذكرتموه لا يوجب التعين . الثاني : إن اختصاص هذا التعين بهذا المتعين دون ذاك ، واختصاص ذلك التعين بذلك المتعين دون هذا : مشروط بامتياز هذا التعين عن ذلك التعين . فلو كان ذلك الامتياز معللاً بحصول هذه الصفة في هذا ، وحصول تلك الصفة في ذلك ، لزم الدور ، وهو محال . الثالث : لو كان تعين هذا المتعين زائداً عليه ، لكان هذا المتعين موجودين ، لا موجوداً واحداً . ثم يكون لكل واحد منهما تعين آخر ، فتصير أربعة لا واحداً . وبهذا الطريق يلزم أن يكون الموجود الواحد غير واحد ، بل موجودات غير متناهية . وهو محال
The second objection: Why is it not permissible that the souls were multiple in pre-eternity? His statement: 'Multiplicity does not occur except for a meaning that necessitates distinction.' We said: This is denied. And there are proofs for it: The first: If determinate individuality (ta'ayyun) were something additional to the essence, and individualities are equal in the quiddity that they are individuality, then it would be necessary that the individuality of each individuality be additional to it, leading to infinite regress. And it cannot be said: Why is it not permissible to say that the quiddity of blackness and the quiddity of individuality, when each one is joined to the other, each one necessitates the individuality of the other? Because we say: The quiddity of blackness is a universal quiddity, and the quiddity of individuality is also a universal quiddity, and if a universal is restricted by a universal, it remains universal and does not become particular. So it is established that what you mention does not necessitate individuality. The second: That the specification of this individuality to this particular individual to the exclusion of that, and the specification of that individuality to that particular individual to the exclusion of this, is conditional upon the distinction of this individuality from that individuality. So if that distinction were caused by the occurrence of this attribute in this one and that attribute in that one, circularity would follow, which is impossible. The third: If the individuality of this particular individual were additional to it, then this particular individual would be two existents, not one existent. Then each of them would have another individuality, so they would become four, not one. And by this reasoning, it necessarily follows that the one existent is not one, but rather infinite existents. And that is impossible.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage presents a second objection and its refutation through three logical arguments. The objection claims that souls could have been multiple in pre-eternity. The responder begins by quoting the objector's principle: multiplicity only occurs due to a meaning that necessitates distinction. The responder denies this principle and provides three proofs. The first proof argues that if determinate individuality (ta'ayyun) were an added attribute to the essence, and all individualities share the same quiddity of being individuality, then each individuality would require another individuality ad infinitum, leading to infinite regress. The objector might propose that the quiddity of blackness and the quiddity of individuality mutually necessitate each other's individuality, but the responder explains that since both quiddities are universals, combining them leaves them universal, not particular. So the proposed solution fails. The second proof addresses the specification of a particular individuality to a particular individual: if this specification depended on a distinction between individualities, and that distinction were caused by attributes in each, then circularity arises because the distinction would presuppose the very attributes it is supposed to explain. The third proof shows that if individuality is additional to the individual, then the individual becomes two existents (essence plus individuality), each requiring its own individuality, leading to four, and by repetition to infinite existents, which is absurd. Thus all three arguments refute the objection.

تسلسل
ماهية
كلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Adding an attribute of individuality can solve the problem of individuation without leading to regress.
Correction: If individuality is an added attribute, each instance of that attribute would require another, leading to an infinite regress. Moreover, combining universals does not produce particularity.

Checkpoint
What logical problem does the first argument identify if individuality is an added attribute?
A) Circularity
B) Infinite regress
C) Contradiction
D) Improper conversion

Key Takeaway
Adding an attribute of individuality to each individual leads to an infinite regress of attributes, making the proposal untenable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what ways do you build your identity on attributes that themselves seem to need further justification? What is the one true source that stops the regress of your self-definition?
?
The objector tried to combine two universals to make a particular. Reflect: Are you trying to construct a meaningful identity by combining worldly abstractions (status, wealth, opinions) that are ultimately universal and empty? How does grounding your identity in your Creator alone make you truly particular?
?
If infinite regress is impossible, what does that mean for the things you chase after (goals, possessions, relationships) that each demand another? What would it look like to anchor your life in the One who requires no further cause?

The Second Proof: Circularity in Specification
Second argument against the second objection: circularity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second refutation: that the specification of a particular individuality to a particular individual leads to circularity if that specification depends on a distinction that itself requires the same attributes.

Core Idea
Specification of individuality cannot rely on a distinction that already assumes what needs to be explained.

The second argument attacks the problem of how a particular individuality becomes attached to a particular individual. The objector must account for why this individuality belongs to this individual and not that one. The responder shows that any attempt to explain this via attributes in each individual leads to circularity (dawr). This lesson explains that logical flaw.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the second argument segment. Note the structure: 'إن اختصاص هذا التعين بهذا المتعين...'.
2
Understand the conditional
The specification of individuality to a particular individual is conditional upon the distinction between individualities. Think about what that means.
The word 'مشروط' indicates conditionality.
3
Identify the circularity
If the distinction is caused by attributes in each individual, then those attributes would have to exist before the individuality they are supposed to explain, leading to a circle.
The term 'دور' (circularity) is key.
4
Confirm impossibility
The passage concludes that circularity is impossible. Reflect on why a circular explanation is invalid.

The Third Proof: Multiplication of Existents
Third argument against the second objection: multiplication of existents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third refutation: that if individuality were an added attribute, each individual would become two existents, leading to an infinite multiplication of existents, which is absurd.

Core Idea
Adding individuality to an essence doubles the existent, and this doubling repeats endlessly.

The third argument shows a devastating consequence: if individuality is extra to the essence, then each individual becomes two things (essence and individuality), each of which would require its own individuality, leading to four, then eight, ad infinitum. This lesson demonstrates that the one existent would become infinite, which is impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the third argument. Notice the reasoning: 'لو كان تعين هذا المتعين زائداً عليه، لكان هذا المتعين موجودين، لا موجوداً واحداً'.
2
Follow the multiplication
If the individual has an added individuality, then the individual becomes two existents. Each of those two would need another individuality, making four. Continue to see infinite regress.
The passage says 'ثم يكون لكل واحد منهما تعين آخر، فتصير أربعة لا واحداً'.
3
Generalize the reasoning
By the same reasoning, the one existent would become infinitely many existents. That is impossible.
The conclusion: 'وبذلك الطريق يلزم أن يكون الموجود الواحد غير واحد، بل موجودات غير متناهية'.
4
Reflect on the absurdity
Consider why infinite multiplication of a single entity is logically unacceptable in this context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Third Objection: Distinction Through Essence Itself
Third objection: distinction may be through essence itself, with incomplete response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third objection against the need for a separate meaning for distinction, and the beginning of the response rejecting the premise of equal quiddity of souls.

Core Idea
The objector asks why distinction cannot be through essence itself; the responder denies the premise of equal quiddity.

In this objection, the opponent concedes that a meaning (attribute) is necessary for distinction, but suggests that meaning could be the essence itself. The responder counters by challenging the underlying assumption that human souls share the same quiddity, asserting that the opponent has no proof for that premise while the responder has many proofs against it.

3
Analyze the response
The responder attacks the premise that souls are equal in essence. Notice that the responder claims to have proofs against it, but the text cuts off before completing the argument.
4

The passage ends mid-sentence. This indicates that the full argument is not given here; further pages are needed.
