The Chosen View: The Celestial Soul
Sanusi presents his view on the celestial soul's nature and functions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's positive description of the celestial soul as a simple substance with both universal and particular perceptions and volitions.

Core Idea
The celestial soul combines simplicity with full perception.

After refuting the opponent, the author presents his own view: the celestial soul is a simple substance free from corporeality, yet it possesses both particular and universal perceptions and volitions. This allows it to know and worship God, removing all doubts. This lesson explores that view.

Guided Path
1
Read the author's chosen view
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Notice the author states 'the chosen view with me is...' introducing his position.
The celestial soul is distinct from the rational soul discussed earlier.
2
Identify the attributes of the celestial soul
The passage lists: it is a simple substance free from corporeality and its attachments, described by particular perceptions/volitions and universal perceptions/volitions.
It has both types of perception and volition, not just one.
3
Understand the outcome: worship and removal of doubts
Because of these attributes, the celestial soul knows its Lord and intends worship through its movements. This resolves the doubts raised by the opponent.
The author clearly connects the attributes to the resolution of ambiguities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث : إن النفس الناطقة جوهر مجرد . وهي مدبرة لهذا البدن المعين فإما أن تدير هذا البدن بإدراكات كليه وقصد كلي . وإما أن تدبره بإدراكات جزئية وقصد جزئي . فإن كان الأول ، فقد بطل قولكم : إن القصد الكلي لا يصدر عنه أفعال جزئية . وإن كان الثاني ، فقد بطل قولكم : إن الجوهر المجرد لا يكون صاحب الإدراكات الجزئية. وعلى كلا التقديرين ، فإنه يبطل كلامكم . وأقول : حقاً إني شديد التعجب من غفلة هؤلاء الأقوام عن هذه الكلمات الظاهرة . فهذا هو الكلام على دليلهم والمختار عندي : أن النفس الفلكية جوهر مجرد عن الجسمية وعلائقها . هذا ، فإنها موصوفة بالإدراكات الجزئية، والإرادات الجزئية . وكذلك أيضاً موصوفة بالإدراكات الكلية، والإرادات الكلية . فهي عارفة بربها ، وقاصدة بهذه الحركات : عبادة ربها وخالقها ومدبرها. وعلى هذا التقدير ، فقد زالت الشكوك والشبهات. ويتفرع على ما ذكرنا : فروع . وهي : أن المسمى بنفس الكل(١) هي نفس الفلك الأعظم. وذلك لأن سائر الأفلاك موجودة في باطن الفلك الأعظم . فهي كالأجزاء من الفلك الأعظم . ونفوسهـا كالقوى المتشعبة من نفس الفلك الأعظم ، كما أن القوى المتشعبة عن النفس الناطقة الموجودة في كل واحد من الأعضاء المخصوصة كالنتائج والآثار والشعب لجوهر النفس الناطقة . فثبت بما ذكرنا : أن تدبير الحق سبحانه لعالم الأجسام ، إنما ابتدأ من الفلك الأعظم، الذي هو العرش. وذلك الابتداء إنما حصل بواسطة تلك النفس التي هي النفس الفلكية . وأما سائر النفوس الفلكية والعنصرية ، نتائجها وشعبها وأولادها. وإليه الإشارة في الدعاء المشهور وهو قوله عليه السلام : اللهم إني أسألك بمعاقد .. على أركان عرشك ، فالمراد من معاقد العز : هو جوهر تلك النفس الكلية وشعبها ، المنبثة منها في أجزاء العرش .
Third: The rational soul is a simple substance. It is the manager of this specific body. So either it manages this body by universal perceptions and universal intention, or it manages it by particular perceptions and particular intention. If the first, then your statement is nullified: that universal intention does not issue in particular actions. And if the second, then your statement is nullified: that the simple substance cannot possess particular perceptions. And on both suppositions, your statement is nullified. And I say: Truly I am greatly astonished at the heedlessness of these people concerning these manifest words. This then is the discussion on their proof. And the chosen view with me is that the celestial soul is a simple substance free from corporeality and its attachments. This is so, for it is described by particular perceptions and particular volitions, and also described by universal perceptions and universal volitions. Thus it knows its Lord, and intends by these movements the worship of its Lord, its Creator, and its Manager. And on this supposition, the doubts and ambiguities have been removed. And there branch from what we have mentioned branches. They are: that what is called the soul of the whole is the soul of the greatest sphere. This is because the other spheres exist in the interior of the greatest sphere. Thus they are like parts of the greatest sphere. And their souls are like the powers branching from the soul of the greatest sphere, just as the powers branching from the rational soul present in each of the particular organs are like the results, traces, and branches of the substance of the rational soul. So it is established by what we have mentioned that the management of the Truth, exalted be He, of the world of bodies began from the greatest sphere, which is the Throne. And that beginning happened by means of that soul which is the celestial soul. As for the other celestial and elemental souls, they are its results, branches, and children. And to this points the well-known supplication, his saying, peace be upon him: 'O Allah, I ask You by the ties of glory upon the pillars of Your Throne.' So what is meant by the ties of glory is the substance of that universal soul and its branches, spread out from it in the parts of the Throne.
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage is a proof combined with a statement of the author's chosen view. The author begins by positing the rational soul as a simple substance that manages the body. He presents a dilemma: either the soul manages with universal perceptions and intention, or with particular perceptions and intention. If the first, then universal intention can produce particular actions, which refutes the opponent who claimed it cannot. If the second, then a simple substance can have particular perceptions, refuting the opponent who denied that. Either way the opponent's position is invalidated. The author then expresses his astonishment at their oversight and presents his own view: the celestial soul is a simple substance free from corporeality, and it possesses both particular and universal perceptions and volitions, allowing it to know God and worship Him through its movements. This resolves doubts. He then elaborates a branch: the soul of the whole is the soul of the greatest sphere (the Throne). Other spheres are like parts, and their souls are like powers branching from that soul, analogous to the powers branching from the human rational soul. Thus, God's management of the physical world begins from the Throne via that celestial soul. Other souls are its offshoots. He concludes by referencing a prophetic supplication, interpreting 'the ties of glory' as that universal soul and its branches.

جوهر مجرد
الإدراكات الجزئية
الإدراكات الكلية

?

?
Sanusi claims that his view removes all doubts. What doubt about the nature of your own soul or its purpose do you still harbor? If you truly believed your soul is a simple substance free from corporeality, how would your attachment to material comforts change right now?

The Celestial Hierarchy: Soul of the Greatest Sphere
Sanusi explains the hierarchy of celestial souls centered on the Throne.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hierarchical relationship between the celestial soul of the greatest sphere (the Throne) and other celestial souls.

Core Idea
The soul of the greatest sphere is the source of all other souls.

The author elaborates on the branches of his view: the soul of the whole (al-nafs al-kull) is the soul of the greatest sphere, which is the Throne. Other spheres are like parts, and their souls are like branching powers from that universal soul. This establishes that God's management of the physical world begins from the Throne via that celestial soul, and other souls are its offshoots. The author also references a prophetic supplication to support this.

Guided Path
1
Identify the 'soul of the whole'
Read the Arabic passage. Find where the author defines 'the soul of the whole' as the soul of the greatest sphere (the Throne).
The greatest sphere is identified with the Throne (al-‘arsh).
2
Understand the hierarchical relationship
Other spheres exist inside the greatest sphere, like parts. Their souls are like powers branching from the soul of the greatest sphere, analogous to the powers branching from the human rational soul to organs.
This is a clear part-whole analogy.
3
Grasp the implication for divine management
God's management of the physical world begins from the Throne via that celestial soul. Other celestial and elemental souls are its results, branches, and children.
The Throne is the starting point of divine administration.
4
Examine the supplication reference
The author quotes a well-known supplication about 'the ties of glory upon the pillars of Your Throne' and interprets 'the ties of glory' as the substance of the universal soul and its branches spread in the parts of the Throne.
This scriptural reference supports his metaphysical model.

Each Intellect as a Unique Species: The Rational Proof
The author presents and critiques the claim that each intellect is a unique species.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' argument that each immaterial intellect must be its own species, and how the author addresses the scriptural objection that angels share functions.

Core Idea
Immaterial beings cannot be individuated by matter, so each intellect is a unique species.

The philosophers argued that angels, being immaterial, cannot share a species because individuation requires matter. This lesson unpacks that logical argument and the author's response to a potential scriptural counterexample.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Let the author's own argumentative flow come through.
The passage is a self-contained argument with a claim, proof, objection, and reply.
2
Understand the logical argument
Identify the conditional reasoning: if two intellects were under one species, they would need matter to be distinct. Since they are immaterial, each must be a unique species.
This is a reductio ad absurdum argument.
3
Analyze the objection and response
The objection from scripture mentions angels with different functions. The author replies that sharing effects does not imply sharing quiddities. Consider why this response is consistent with the proof.
The author does not fully endorse the philosophers' claim; he presents it as part of their system.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفرع الثاني : قالوا : كل واحد من هذه العقول ، يجب أن يكون نوعه في شخصه . لأنا لو فرضنا [ وجود شخصين (۱) ] منها تحت نوع واحد ، فامتياز أحدهما عن الآخر . لا يكون بالماهية ولا بلوازمها ، فوجب أن يكون بسبب اختلاف المواد. فيلزم : أن يصير المجرد عن المادة متعلقاً بالمادة . هذا خلف . وأما الذي جاء في الكتاب الإلهي في أن بعضها و صافات ، وبعضها ه زاجرات ، وبعضها و تاليات ، فلا يخالف ذلك الكلام . لما بينا : أن الاشتراك في اللوازم والآثار ، لا يدل على الاشتراك في الماهيات [ وبالله التوفيق (۲) ] .
The second branch: They said: Each one of these intellects must be its species in its person. For if we assumed two individuals under one species, then the distinction of one from the other would not be by quiddity nor by its necessary concomitants, so it would have to be due to difference of matters. Then it would follow that the immaterial becomes attached to matter. This is a contradiction. As for what came in the divine book that some of them are standing, some are restraining, and some are reciting, that does not contradict this statement. Because we have made clear that sharing in the necessary concomitants and effects does not indicate sharing in the quiddities. And with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage addresses the claim that each intellect (angel) must be a unique species, meaning that no two angels share the same species—each one is an individual species. The philosophers argue that if there were two individuals under one species, their distinction would require matter, but they are immaterial; thus it is impossible. The author then anticipates an objection from scripture, which describes angels with different functions (standing, restraining, reciting). He argues that sharing effects does not imply sharing quiddities, so the scriptural descriptions do not contradict the philosophers' claim—or rather, the author is reporting their view and seemingly not fully endorsing it. The passage ends with 'and with Allah is success,' indicating the author's reliance on divine guidance. This is a succinct logical argument that uses the principle of individuation: immaterial beings cannot be individuated by matter, so each must be a distinct species. The author presents it as part of the philosophers' system, likely to critique it later or show its implications.

Key Terms
نوع (species)
شخص (individual)
ماهية (quiddity)
مادة (matter)
لوازم (necessary concomitants)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sharing functions (like standing, restraining) implies that angels share a species.
Correction: The author clarifies that sharing effects or necessary concomitants does not indicate sharing quiddities. So different functions do not prove a common species.

Checkpoint
According to the philosophers, why must each intellect be its own species?
A) Because they differ in their functions.
B) Because if there were two under one species, their distinction would require matter, which is impossible for immaterial beings.
C) Because God creates each one uniquely.
D) Because they are created at different times.

Key Takeaway
Immaterial intellects cannot share a species because their individuation does not depend on matter, so each is a unique species.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If each immaterial intellect is a unique species created by Allah with a distinct essence, what does that imply about your own soul? Are you merely a generic individual, or do you have a unique purpose that no one else can fulfill? How would you live differently today if you truly believed your soul is a unique species for which you alone are responsible?
?
The author ends the argument with 'and with Allah is success,' acknowledging that human reasoning is limited and ultimate reliance is on Allah. In what area of your life have you been relying solely on your own logic or efforts, neglecting to say 'and with Allah is success'? What would it look like to hand that area over to Him today?
?
This lesson argues that immaterial beings cannot be individuated by matter. Your identity is often tied to your body, appearance, and material possessions. But if your soul is immaterial and unique, what does that say about how you should view and care for your soul versus your body? Are you investing more in your material existence or in your immaterial soul's uniqueness? What is one concrete change you can make this week to prioritize your soul's unique purpose over material concerns?

The Four-Fold Order of Divine Mercy
The author establishes the hierarchical order of divine mercy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hierarchical chain of divine mercy as described by the author, and its implications for the relative ranks of angels and prophets.

Core Idea
Divine mercy flows from God through angels, books, and finally to prophets.

This passage presents a structured argument about how divine mercy reaches creation. The author establishes a four-tier hierarchy that not only explains the process but also implies a ranking of beings. Before we read the passage, consider: if mercy comes from God, who or what conveys it? And who receives it? The author answers these questions in a logical order.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the four-part structure: first, second, third, fourth.
2
Identify the four elements
Identify the four stages: the origin (God), the intermediaries (angels), the benefits (books), and the receivers (prophets). How does the author order them?
3
Understand the logical necessity
The author says 'فلا بد أولاً من الأصل...' – why is this order necessary? Think about the flow from source to receiver.
4
Reflect on the implication for rank
The passage concludes that this order indicates the most excellent in rank. Who is ranked highest after God? What does this imply about angels vs. prophets? This is a key theological point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالكتب ، وربع بالرسل . وهذا الترتيب في غاية الصحة والفائدة. لأن منبع النور والكمال والرحمة هو الله تعالى. والوسائط هم الملائكة . والقابل لتلك الرحمة هم الأنبياء والرسل. فلا بد أولاً من الأصل ، وثانياً من الواسطة وثالثاً من حصول تلك الرحمة ، ورابعا من وصولها إلى القابل ، وهم الأنبياء والرسل . وهذا يدل على أن أفضل الموجودات في الشرف [ والرتبة هو الله تعالى ، وبعده في المرتبة درجات الملائكة ، وبعدهم في الشرف (۱) ] تلك الفوائد والأنوار [ التي هي الكتب . وفي آخر الدرجات : الأرواح البشرية التي لما وصلت إليها تلك الفوائد والأنوار [؟] سعدت بها ، وكملت فضائلها بسببها.
With the books, and a fourth with the messengers. This arrangement is extremely sound and beneficial. Because the source of light, perfection, and mercy is Allah Almighty. The intermediaries are the angels. The receivers of that mercy are the prophets and messengers. So first there must be the origin, second the intermediary, third the attainment of that mercy, and fourth its reaching the receiver, who are the prophets and messengers. This indicates that the most excellent of existing things in honor and rank is Allah Almighty, and after Him in rank are the degrees of angels, and after them in honor are those benefits and lights which are the books. And at the last degree are the human souls, which, when those benefits and lights reached them, became happy by them and their virtues were perfected by them.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage presents a four-tier hierarchy in the transmission of divine mercy. The author begins by stating that the order—books and a fourth with messengers—is extremely sound. He explains: the source (الله تعالى) is the fountainhead of light, perfection, and mercy; the intermediaries (الوسائط) are the angels; the receivers (القابل) are the prophets and messengers. Thus there must be: first the origin, second the intermediary, third the attainment of mercy, and fourth its arrival to the receiver. This order implies that in honor and rank, منزلة, the best is God, then the angels, then the books (which contain the benefits and lights), and finally the human souls (prophets) who receive those lights. The argument by arrangement suggests the superiority of angels over prophets, as prophets are receivers and angels are intermediaries closer to the source.

Key Terms
الملائكة
الأنبياء
الرسل
الوسائط
الفوائد والأنوار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets are the highest creation after God.
Correction: This passage indicates that angels rank above prophets because they are the intermediaries closer to the source of mercy, while prophets are receivers at the end of the chain.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the role of angels in the hierarchy of divine mercy?
A) They are the ultimate source of mercy.
B) They are the intermediaries between God and the prophets.
C) They are the receivers of mercy.
D) They are the books themselves.

Key Takeaway
Divine mercy flows from Allah through angels to books, and finally to prophets, making angels intermediaries higher in rank than prophets.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson shows that the flow of mercy from Allah to the prophets passes through angels and books. How often do you consciously thank Allah for the angels and the scriptures He has placed as means of His mercy? Will you today pause and express gratitude for these intermediaries?
?
The hierarchy places angels above prophets in rank. Does this unsettle your reverence for the prophets? How does knowing that the prophets themselves received mercy through angels affect your trust in the divine order? What does it require of you to accept this ranking with full submission?
?
If Allah is the sole source of mercy, why does He use intermediaries? In your own life, do you sometimes seek mercy through created means (people, status, wealth) while forgetting that they are only channels? What would it look like for you to rely entirely on Allah while still honoring the means He has appointed?

intermediate
6 min
The 19 Bodily Forces Opposing the Rational Soul
Enumerates 19 bodily forces opposing the rational soul, cites Quran, concludes human intellect is weak.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author argues that the human rational soul is weakened by nineteen bodily forces, and why this implies a fundamental difference between human and celestial intellects.

Core Idea
The rational soul is overwhelmed by 19 bodily forces, making human intellect weak compared to celestial intelligences.

In this passage, the author continues his series of arguments by presenting a seventh proof based on the internal conflict within human beings. He enumerates the forces that oppose the rational faculty and then draws a stark contrast with the pure, unimpeded intellects of celestial beings. This lesson will walk you through the enumeration and the argument's conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the author's systematic enumeration and his use of a Quranic verse.
Pay attention to how he categorizes the forces.
2
Identify the four categories of bodily forces
The author lists nineteen forces divided into four groups. Find each group and note the specific forces mentioned.
The external senses, internal senses, desire/anger, and vegetative forces.
3
Understand the Quranic reference
The author cites verse 74:30 ('Over it are nineteen') and interprets 'Hell' as the hell of the body. Reflect on this metaphorical interpretation.
This supports his claim that bodily forces dominate from birth.
4
Follow the argument to its conclusion
The author argues that the rational faculty appears late, after bodily forces are entrenched, and is unsupported. Hence, its light is weak. Contrast this with celestial souls.
The final rhetorical question challenges any notion of similarity between humans and angels.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والسابع : إن الإنسان، وإن حصلت له القوة العاقلة المدركة، إلا أنها معارضة بتسعة عشر نوعاً من القوى الجسمانية وكلها تضاد القوة العقلية في تحصيل الكمالات الروحانية . فالحواس الظاهرة متوجهة إلى كيفية الجسمانيات، ومعرضة عن الروحانيات. وأما الحواس الخمسة الباطنة، فهي مشتغلة بضبط تلك الأحوال التي اكتسبتها الحواس الظاهرة بالتصرف فيها . وأما الشهوة والغضب، فالحال بكونهما مانعين من الأحوال الروحانية في غاية الظهور . وأما القوى السبعة النباتية: وهي : الجاذبة والدافعة والغاذية والنامية والمولدة فظاهر أنها مانعة من الالتفات إلى عالم الروحانيات ولهذا السبب جاء في الكتاب الإلهي : إن جهنم لها تسعة عشر عدداً من الزبانية فقد قال تعالى : ( عليها تسعة عشر ) والمراد منه : جهنم البدن . وهي مستولية على البدن من أول التكوين والحدوث إلى آخره . وأما القوة العقلية فهي إنما تلوح بعد البلوغ، وبعد رسوخ القوى الجسمانية في البدن، واستيلائها عليه . ثم إنها مجردة عن الأعوان والأنصار . وإذا كان الأمر كذلك، فحينئذ يظهر أن نور القوة العاقلة في جواهر النفوس الناطقة : يكون ضعيفاً . وأما النفوس الفلكية والعقول المجردة، فهي في ذواتها، أعلى من أن يقال : إنها أنوار. وأما معارفها فهي التعقلات الكاملة المشرقة المتعالية عن ظلمات القوى الجسمانية، وأوضار القوى الطبيعية الغاذية والهاضمة والدافعة فكيف يخطر ببال العاقل : إثبات مناسبة بين البابين ؟ وههنا آخر الكلام في هذه المقالة . والله أعلم . تمت المقالة الخامسة . والحمد الله كما هو أهله . والصلاة والسلام على محمد وآله وصحبه وليكن ههنا آخر كلامنا في شرح الأحوال العالية والسافلة .
And the seventh: Indeed man, even if he possesses the rational perceiving faculty, it is opposed by nineteen types of bodily forces, all of which oppose the rational faculty in acquiring spiritual perfections. The external senses are directed towards the modality of bodily things and are turned away from spiritual things. As for the five internal senses, they are occupied with regulating those states acquired by the external senses by disposing of them. As for desire and anger, the fact that they are preventers of spiritual states is extremely apparent. As for the seven vegetative forces: they are the attractive, expulsive, nutritive, growth, and reproductive forces; it is apparent that they prevent turning towards the world of spiritualities. For this reason, it came in the Divine Book that Hell has nineteen gatekeepers; Allah Most High said: (Over it are nineteen). And the intended meaning of that is the Hell of the body. And it dominates the body from the beginning of formation and origination to its end. As for the rational faculty, it only appears after puberty, and after the bodily forces have become established in the body and have dominated it. Then it is devoid of helpers and supporters. And if such is the case, then it becomes clear that the light of the rational faculty in the substances of the speaking souls is weak. As for the celestial souls and the abstract intellects, they in their essences are too high to be called lights. And as for their cognitions, they are the complete, shining intellections that are transcendent over the darknesses of bodily forces and the impurities of natural forces: the nutritive, digestive, and expulsive. So how could a rational person conceive of establishing any proportion between the two categories? And here is the end of the discourse in this article. And Allah knows best. Completed is the fifth article. And praise be to Allah as is His due. And blessings and peace be upon Muhammad and his family and his companions. And let here be the end of our words in explaining the exalted and lowly states.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh argument in a series, likely aimed at refuting the notion that prophets are superior to angels. The author argues that the human rational faculty, although present, is opposed by nineteen types of bodily forces, which collectively obstruct the acquisition of spiritual perfections. He then enumerates these forces: first, the five external senses, which are preoccupied with bodily things; second, the five internal senses, which manage the impressions from the external senses; third, desire and anger, which clearly prevent spiritual states; and fourth, the seven vegetative forces (attractive, expulsive, nutritive, growth, and reproductive), which divert attention from the spiritual world. The author supports this by citing the Quranic verse 'Over it are nineteen' (74:30), interpreting 'Hell' as the bodily hell that dominates from birth. The rational faculty emerges only after puberty, after the bodily forces are already entrenched and unsupported. Consequently, the light of the rational soul is weak. In contrast, celestial souls and abstract intellects are inherently superior, their intelligences being complete and free from bodily impurities. Therefore, it is irrational to claim any similarity between humans and celestial beings. The passage concludes the fifth article of the work.

Key Terms
القوة العاقلة
القوى الجسمانية
النفوس الفلكية
العقول المجردة
جهنم البدن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author completely denies the value of human intellect.
Correction: The author does not deny human intellect; he only compares it to the far superior celestial intellects, showing that human intellect is relatively weak, not worthless.

Checkpoint
How many types of bodily forces oppose the rational faculty according to the seventh argument?
A) Five
B) Twelve
C) Nineteen
D) Seven

Key Takeaway
The human rational soul is weakened by nineteen bodily forces, making it incomparably inferior to the pure intellects of celestial beings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just read that your rational soul is opposed by 19 bodily forces. Which of these forces do you feel most dominating your own pursuit of spiritual knowledge today? Write down one specific step you will take to weaken its hold on you this week.
?
The author says the rational faculty appears only after puberty and is unsupported. Reflect: Are you actively supporting your intellect against bodily forces, or have you allowed it to remain weak? What one habit could strengthen it starting today?
?
The verse 'Over it are nineteen' is interpreted as the Hell of the body. In what ways is your body a 'hell' that holds you back from spiritual perfection? Be honest before Allah—what is one bodily desire you will struggle against tomorrow?
